<p><b>Hurricane Maria</b> is a strong <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclone</a> which struck <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> as a Category&#160;5 hurricane on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> as a Category&#160;4 hurricane, and is currently threatening <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a> and parts of the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Mid-Atlantic United States">Mid-Atlantic</a>. It is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_most_intense_tropical_cyclones#North_Atlantic_Ocean" title="List of the most intense tropical cyclones">tenth-most intense Atlantic hurricane on record</a>, and the worst to strike Puerto Rico since <a href="/wiki/1928_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1928 Atlantic hurricane season">1928</a>. The thirteenth <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">named storm</a>, seventh <a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a>, fourth <a href="/wiki/Major_hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Major hurricane">major hurricane</a>, and the second Category&#160;5 hurricane of the unusually active <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017 Atlantic hurricane season</a>, Maria caused catastrophic damage during its journey across the Northeastern Caribbean. It was the third major hurricane in a row to threaten the Leeward Islands with a direct strike or major impacts within two weeks, after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> caused catastrophic damage there and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Jose</a>, then a Category&#160;4 hurricane, passed dangerously close just days after.</p>
<p>Originating from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> began monitoring on September 13, Maria developed into a tropical storm on September 16 east of the Lesser Antilles, with steady strengthening occurring. In remarkably favorable conditions for further development, on September 18, Maria underwent <a href="/wiki/Explosive_intensification" class="mw-redirect" title="Explosive intensification">explosive intensification</a>, doubling its sustained wind speed from 80&#160;mph (130&#160;km/h) to 160&#160;mph (260&#160;km/h), becoming a Category&#160;5 hurricane, making the 2017 season the first since <a href="/wiki/2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2007 Atlantic hurricane season">2007</a> to feature two Category&#160;5 hurricanes, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes#Systems" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">one of only six Atlantic hurricane seasons</a> to feature two or more Category&#160;5 hurricanes in the satellite era. When Maria made landfall at this strength at <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> the following day, it became the first Category&#160;5 hurricane to strike Dominica, and made 2017 the second season (after 2007) to feature two hurricanes making landfall at Category&#160;5 intensity. After briefly weakening to Category&#160;4 status, Maria reintensified to attain peak winds of 175&#160;mph (280&#160;km/h) and a minimum central pressure of 908&#160;mbar (hPa; 26.85&#160;inHg), becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_intense_tropical_cyclones#North_Atlantic_Ocean" class="mw-redirect" title="List of most intense tropical cyclones">tenth most intense Atlantic hurricane</a> on record. For 2017, this central pressure is the lowest worldwide thus far. Succeeding peak intensity, an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> caused Maria to weaken to a high-end Category&#160;4 hurricane with winds of 155&#160;mph (250&#160;km/h) before making landfall in Puerto Rico, making Maria the strongest to hit the territory since the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 San Felipe hurricane</a>, as well as the most intense hurricane (in terms of central pressure) to hit the territory in recorded history, and the most intense to make landfall anywhere in the United States (including locations outside of the <a href="/wiki/Contiguous_United_States" title="Contiguous United States">Lower 48</a>) since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">Hurricane Camille</a> in 1969.</p>
<p>As of September 25, the hurricane has caused at least 59 deaths: 27 in <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, 3 in <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, 24 in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, and 1 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands" title="United States Virgin Islands">United States Virgin Islands</a>. Initial assessments indicate catastrophic damage to Dominica, which suffered an island-wide communication blackout. The islands of Guadeloupe and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> also endured widespread flooding, damaged roofs and uprooted trees. Puerto Rico was left without electric power, its electrical grid having been effectively destroyed.</p>
<p></p>

<h2>Contents</h2>
</div>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meteorological_history">Meteorological history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Meteorological history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/220px-Maria_2017_track.png" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/330px-Maria_2017_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Maria_2017_track.png/440px-Maria_2017_track.png 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1907" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_2017_track.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map plotting the track and intensity of the storm according to the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC) began monitoring two <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical waves</a> on September 13.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The easternmost wave quickly spun up into what would become <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Lee" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">Hurricane Lee</a>, while the western one continued moving generally west. With generally favorable conditions in the disturbance's path, development into a tropical cyclone seemed likely.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> During those two days the disturbance became better organized,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and by September 16, <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">convective banding</a> became established around a poorly organized circulation. As the system was an imminent threat to land despite the center not being well-defined, the NHC initiated advisories on it as "Potential Tropical Cyclone Fifteen" at 15:00&#160;UTC, in accordance with a policy change enacted at the start of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-D1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> A mid-level <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> anchored north of the disturbance steered it generally west-northwest into a region highly favorable for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclogenesis" title="Tropical cyclogenesis">further development</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">Sea surface temperatures</a> of 84&#160;°F (29&#160;°C), low <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, and ample moisture were anticipated to foster strengthening to hurricane-status before the system reached the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-D1_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-D4_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D4-6">[6]</a></sup> As the disturbance continued to grow increasingly well-defined throughout the day, it was later upgraded to a moderate-range tropical storm – based on satellite estimates – at 21:00&#160;UTC that day, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">receiving the name</a> <i>Maria</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> At this time, Maria was situated 620&#160;mi (1,000&#160;km) east-southeast of the Lesser Antilles.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>

<th>10</th>
<td><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Maria</a></td>

<td>26.81</td>
</tr>
<tr class="small">
<th colspan="6">Source: HURDAT<sup id="cite_ref-HURDAT_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-9">[9]</a></sup></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> and favorable <a href="/wiki/Outflow_(meteorology)" title="Outflow (meteorology)">outflow</a> developed atop the center of circulation, which enabled Maria to become further organized throughout the early morning hours of September 17.<sup id="cite_ref-D4_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D4-6">[6]</a></sup> After a brief intrusion of dry air exposed the circulation,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> a convective burst occurred over the center and intensification resumed. <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hunters" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Hunters">Hurricane Hunters</a> investigating the system observed surface winds of 74&#160;mph (119&#160;km/h) and a formative <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> feature. Accordingly, the NHC upgraded Maria to hurricane status at 21:00&#160;UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Expansion of the central dense overcast and an increasingly complete eyewall signaled steady intensification throughout the overnight of September&#160;17–18.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Considerable <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> activity was identified within the hurricane's core early on September&#160;18 and statistical models indicated a high probability of <a href="/wiki/Rapid_intensification" title="Rapid intensification">rapid intensification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Explosive strengthening took place shortly thereafter, with aircraft reconnaissance finding surface winds of 120&#160;mph (190&#160;km/h) and a central pressure of 959&#160;mbar (hPa; 28.32&#160;inHg), making Maria a Category&#160;3 hurricane on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a>, and hence a major hurricane. Additionally, radar data revealed a well-defined 12&#160;mi (19&#160;km) wide eye.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The eye contracted slightly to 9&#160;mi (14&#160;km) as intensification continued, and the system reached Category&#160;4 strength by 21:00&#160;UTC.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/220px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/330px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png/440px-Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png 2x" data-file-width="693" data-file-height="616" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Composite_Reflectivity_San_Juan_radar_92017.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Radar imagery of Hurricane Maria from Puerto Rico at 09:36&#160;UTC (5:36&#160;a.m. local time), shortly before it stopped transmitting data.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rapid intensification culminated late September&#160;18 with Maria achieving Category&#160;5 status just 15&#160;mi (25&#160;km) east-southeast of Dominica.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Hurricane Hunters observed surface winds of 160&#160;mph (260&#160;km/h) and a pressure of 925&#160;mbar (hPa; 27.32&#160;inHg) at this time.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Maria made <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfall</a> in Dominica at 01:15&#160;UTC on September&#160;19,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> becoming the first Category&#160;5 hurricane on record to strike the island nation.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Interaction with the mountains of Dominica imparted slight weakening of the hurricane to Category&#160;4; however, once over the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> Maria regained Category&#160;5 intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Additional strengthening took place as the storm tracked northwest toward <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Despite the formation of concentric eyewalls—the larger one spanning 25 to 35&#160;mi (40 to 56&#160;km) and the smaller only 5&#160;mi (8.0&#160;km), signalling the start of an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>—the inner violent core remained undisrupted through the afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Maria attained its peak intensity around 03:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;20, roughly 30&#160;mi (45&#160;km) south of <a href="/wiki/St._Croix" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Croix">St. Croix</a>. Sustained winds reached 175&#160;mph (280&#160;km/h) and its central pressure bottomed out at 908&#160;mbar (hPa; 26.85&#160;inHg); this ranks it as the tenth-strongest Atlantic hurricane since reliable records began.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/220px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/330px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif/440px-Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maria_GOES_Floater_Rainbow_IR_0925EDT_20-Sept-2017.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Infrared loop of Hurricane Maria passing St.&#160;Croix, Vieques, and landfalling on Puerto Rico on the morning of September 20</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The hurricane made its closest approach to St. Croix around 05:00&#160;UTC on September&#160;20, passing within 20&#160;mi (30&#160;km) of the island; the storm's outer eyewall lashed the island while the more violent inner eye remained offshore.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Hours later, around 08:00&#160;UTC, the outer eyewall struck <a href="/wiki/Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieques">Vieques</a>, an island off the eastern coast of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> By this time, the outer eye became dominant as the inner one decayed, and the eyewall replacement cycle caused Maria to weaken to Category&#160;4 strength.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Maria made landfall just south of <a href="/wiki/Yabucoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Yabucoa">Yabucoa</a>, Puerto Rico, around 10:15&#160;UTC with sustained winds of 155&#160;mph (250&#160;km/h),<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> making it the strongest to hit the island since the <a href="/wiki/1928_Okeechobee_hurricane" title="1928 Okeechobee hurricane">1928 San Felipe Segundo hurricane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Maria maintained a general west-northwest course across Puerto Rico, emerging over the Atlantic Ocean shortly before 18:00&#160;UTC. Interaction with the mountainous terrain resulted in substantial weakening; sustained winds fell to 110&#160;mph (175&#160;km/h) and the central pressure rose to 957&#160;mbars (hPa; 28.26&#160;inHg).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> With favorable environmental conditions, Maria steadily reorganized as it moved away from Puerto Rico. A large eye, 45&#160;mi (75&#160;km) wide, developed with deep convection blossoming around it. Early on September&#160;21, the system regained Category&#160;3 intensity.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, cooler waters <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">stirred up</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> two weeks prior limited Maria's reorganization.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> During the afternoon of September&#160;21, the system traversed the <a href="/wiki/Navidad_Bank" title="Navidad Bank">Navidad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Silver_Bank" title="Silver Bank">Silver</a> banks north of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Wave_shoaling" title="Wave shoaling">shoaling</a> from the region's shallow waters temporarily interfered with measurements of surface winds.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Convection around the storm's eye deepened and its eye became better defined that night, and the hurricane reached a tertiary peak with sustained winds of 125&#160;mph (205&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> An increase in southwesterly wind shear prompted gradual weakening of the hurricane, starting with restriction of banding features and later degradation of the eyewall.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Late on September&#160;22, the hurricane turned north-northwest as it reached the western periphery of the ridge previously steering it northwest.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Maria fluctuated in organization throughout September&#160;23, with its eye periodically clearing and becoming cloud-filled; it maintained Category&#160;3 hurricane strength during this phase.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Despite a decreasing central pressure The storm finally weakened to Category&#160;2 strength early on September&#160;24. Hurricane Hunters observed flight-level winds of 116 to 135&#160;mph (187 to 217&#160;km/h); however, surface wind returns by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.aoml.noaa.gov/hrd/about_hrd/HRD-P3_sfmr.html">Stepped-Frequency Microwave Radiometer</a> were only 90&#160;mph (150&#160;km/h). This indicated blow-average mixing down of winds aloft.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-D34_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D34-42">[42]</a></sup> By this time, Maria's trajectory shifted almost due north between the aforementioned ridge and a <a href="/wiki/Block_(meteorology)#Cut-off_highs_and_lows" title="Block (meteorology)">cut-off low</a> over the eastern <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-D34_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-D34-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Weakening accelerated later on September&#160;24 into September&#160;25 as the hurricane traversed a cold wake—with sea surface temperatures of 75–77&#160;°F (24–25&#160;°C)—created by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Jose_(2017)" title="Hurricane Jose (2017)">Hurricane Jose</a> a week prior. Maria degraded to Category&#160;1 strength during this time.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Early on September&#160;25, Maria's structure changed dramatically as its inner-core collapsed. The low-level circulation became exposed to the northwest and most deep convection shifted to the eastern half of the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_storm_information">Current storm information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Current storm information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 5:00&#160;p.m. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a> (21:00&#160;<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>) September&#160;25, Hurricane Maria is located within 20&#160;nautical miles of <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Hurricane_Maria&amp;params=31.7_N_-73.1_E_&amp;title=Maria"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">31°42′N</span> <span class="longitude">73°06′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="vcard"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">31.7°N 73.1°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">31.7; -73.1</span></span><span style="display:none">﻿ (<span class="fn org">Maria</span>)</span></span></span></a></span>, about 280&#160;miles (450&#160;km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Hatteras,_North_Carolina" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Hatteras, North Carolina">Cape Hatteras, North Carolina</a>. Maximum sustained winds are 70&#160;knots (80&#160;mph; 130&#160;km/h), a Category&#160;1 on the <a href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson scale">Saffir–Simpson scale</a>, with gusts to 85&#160;knots (100&#160;mph; 165&#160;km/h). The minimum barometric pressure is 957&#160;millibars (hPa; 28.26&#160;inHg). The system is moving north at 6&#160;knots (7&#160;mph; 11&#160;km/h). Hurricane-force winds extend outward up to 105&#160;miles (165&#160;km) from the center of Maria, while tropical storm-force winds extended outward up to 205&#160;miles (335&#160;km).</p>
<p>For latest official information, see:</p>
<ul>
<li>The NHC's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCPAT5+shtml/">latest public advisory on Hurricane Maria</a></li>
<li>The NHC's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCMAT5+shtml/">latest forecast advisory on Hurricane Maria</a></li>
<li>The NHC's <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nhc.noaa.gov/text/refresh/MIATCDAT5+shtml/">latest forecast discussion on Hurricane Maria</a></li>
</ul>

The U.S. Navy helps evacuate military personnel from the U.S. Virgin Islands, ahead of Hurricane Maria</div>

<p>Upon the initiation of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> (NHC)'s first advisories for the system that would become Tropical Storm Maria on the morning of September 16, the government of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> issued tropical storm watches for the islands of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, while <a href="/wiki/St._Lucia" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lucia">St. Lucia</a> issued a tropical storm watch for its citizens, and the government of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> issued a similar watch for <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-public_advisory_1_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_1-45">[45]</a></sup>Barbados would later that day declare a tropical storm watch for its citizens and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-public_advisory_1a_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_1a-46">[46]</a></sup> The government of <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a> issued Hurricane watches for the islands of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbuda" title="Barbuda">Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Kitts" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Kitts">St. Kitts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a> by the time of the NHC's second advisory which declared Maria a tropical storm.<sup id="cite_ref-public_advisory_2_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-public_advisory_2-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-washington_post_1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-washington_post_1-48">[48]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> activated the <a href="/wiki/International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters" title="International Charter on Space and Major Disasters">International Charter on Space and Major Disasters</a> for humanitarian satellite coverage on the 20th.<sup id="cite_ref-Dominican_Republic_Activates_the_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dominican_Republic_Activates_the_International_Charter_on_Space_and_Major_Disasters-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Still recovering from Hurricane Irma two weeks prior, approximately 80,000&#160;remained without power as Maria approached.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Electric_Power_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority">Puerto Rico Electric Power Authority</a> (PREPA) struggled with increasing debt, reaching $9&#160;billion even before the hurricanes prompting them to file for bankruptcy. Furthermore, the company lost 30&#160;percent of its employees since 2012. Aging infrastructure across the island makes the grid more susceptible to damage from storms; the median age of PREPA power plants is 44&#160;years. Inadequate safety also plagues the company and local newspapers frequently describe poor maintenance and outdated controls.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Evacuation orders were issued in Puerto Rico in advance of Maria, and officials announced that 450 shelters would open in the afternoon of September&#160;18.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> As of September 19, at least 2,000 people in Puerto Rico have sought shelter.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Southern_Windward_Islands">Southern Windward Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Southern Windward Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The outer <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">rainbands</a> of Maria produced heavy rainfall and strong gusts across the southern <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hewanorra_International_Airport" title="Hewanorra International Airport">Hewanorra</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_F._L._Charles_Airport" title="George F. L. Charles Airport">George F. L. Charles</a> airports of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> respectively recorded 4.33&#160;in (110&#160;mm) and 3.1&#160;in (80&#160;mm) of rain, though even higher quantities fell elsewhere on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Scattered rock slides, landslides and uprooted trees caused minor damage and blocked some roads.<sup id="cite_ref-stluciarock_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stluciarock-62">[62]</a></sup> Several districts experienced localized blackouts due to downed or damaged power lines.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The agricultural sector, especially the banana industry, suffered losses from the winds.<sup id="cite_ref-stluciarock_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stluciarock-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heavy rainfall amounting to 3–5&#160;in (75–125&#160;mm)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> caused scattered flooding across <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>; in <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Barbados" title="Christ Church, Barbados">Christ Church</a>, the flood waters trapped residents from the neighborhood of <a href="/wiki/Christ_Church,_Barbados#Towns.2C_villages.2C_and_hamlets" title="Christ Church, Barbados">Goodland</a> in their homes and inundated the business streets of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_Gap" title="Saint Lawrence Gap">Saint Lawrence Gap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Maria stirred up rough seas that flooded coastal sidewalks in <a href="/wiki/Bridgetown" title="Bridgetown">Bridgetown</a> and damaged boats as operators had difficulties securing their vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> High winds triggered an island-wide power outage and downed a coconut tree onto a residence in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph,_Barbados" title="Saint Joseph, Barbados">Saint Joseph</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5008" data-file-height="3336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_destruction_along_Roseau_road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A road in the <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> area is littered with structural debris, damaged vegetation and downed power poles and lines.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rainfall ahead of the hurricane caused several landslides in Dominica as water levels across the island began to rise by the afternoon of September 18.<sup id="cite_ref-before_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-before-70">[70]</a></sup> Maria made landfall at 21:35 <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Standard_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic Standard Time">AST</a> that day (1:35 <a href="/wiki/UTC" class="mw-redirect" title="UTC">UTC</a>, September 19) as a Category&#160;5 hurricane with winds of 160&#160;mph (260&#160;km/h). The extreme winds blew the roofs off many houses, including the <a href="/wiki/Official_residence" title="Official residence">official residence</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Dominica" title="Prime Minister of Dominica">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Skerrit" title="Roosevelt Skerrit">Roosevelt Skerrit</a>, who required rescue when his home began to flood.<sup id="cite_ref-IBtimes_PM_roof_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBtimes_PM_roof-71">[71]</a></sup> Skerrit called the devastation "mind boggling" and indicated immediate priority was to rescue survivors rather than assess damage.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimedom_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimedom-72">[72]</a></sup> The situation on Dominica remained unclear for at least a day after the hurricane's passage, as downed cellular, radio and internet services effectually cut the island off from the outside world.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimedom_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimedom-72">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Initial radio reports from <a href="/wiki/Roseau" title="Roseau">Roseau</a> on September&#160;19 indicated "total devastation," with half the city flooded, cars stranded, and stretches of residential area "flattened".<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next morning, the first aerial footage began to reveal the scope of the damage on the island. Neighborhoods were littered with structural debris as rows of houses along the entirety of the coastline were rendered uninhabitable. According to initial estimates, the hurricane caused damage to 90% of structures on Dominica, including to the roofs of those that had served as shelters. It devastated the island's <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret_Hospital_(Roseau)" title="Princess Margaret Hospital (Roseau)">primary hospital</a>, compromising the safety of its patients. The population suffered from an island-wide water shortage due to uprooted pipes in Maria's wake.<sup id="cite_ref-Dominicafootage_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dominicafootage-75">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Disaster_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency">Caribbean Disaster Emergency Management Agency</a> (CDEMA) estimates that the hurricane has caused "billions of dollars" worth of damage.<sup id="cite_ref-dominicadamage_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dominicadamage-76">[76]</a></sup> As of September&#160;25, there are 27&#160;fatalities confirmed across the island with another 27&#160;reported missing.<sup id="cite_ref-Dominica27_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dominica27-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Guadeloupe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_(nettoyage_des_routes).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/220px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/330px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg/440px-D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_%28nettoyage_des_routes%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4394" data-file-height="3343" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%A9gats_Ouragan_Maria_(nettoyage_des_routes).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Numerous trees fell across Guadeloupe, clogging roadways with debris</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Blustery conditions spread over <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> as Maria tracked to the south of the archipelago, which endured hours of unabating hurricane-force winds.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The strongest winds blew along the southern coastlines of <a href="/wiki/Basse-Terre_Island" title="Basse-Terre Island">Basse-Terre Island</a>: <a href="/wiki/Gourbeyre" title="Gourbeyre">Gourbeyre</a> observed a peak wind speed of 101 mph (162&#160;km/h), while winds up north in nearby <a href="/wiki/Baillif" title="Baillif">Baillif</a> reached 92&#160;mph (148&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupemeteo_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupemeteo-78">[78]</a></sup> Along those regions, the hurricane kicked up extremely rough seas with 20&#160;ft (6&#160;m) waves.<sup id="cite_ref-waves_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waves-79">[79]</a></sup> The combination of rough seas and winds was responsible for widespread structural damage and flooding throughout the archipelago, especially from Pointe-à-Pitre, along <a href="/wiki/Grande-Terre" title="Grande-Terre">Grand-Terre Island</a>'s southwestern coast, to <a href="/wiki/Petit-Bourg" title="Petit-Bourg">Petit-Bourg</a> and the southern coasts on Basse-Terre Island.<sup id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-57">[57]</a></sup> Aside from wind-related effects, rainfall from Maria was also significant. In just a day, the hurricane dropped nearly a month's worth of rainfall at some important locations: <a href="/wiki/Pointe-%C3%A0-Pitre" title="Pointe-à-Pitre">Pointe-à-Pitre</a> recorded a 24-hour total of 7.5&#160;inches (191&#160;mm), while the capital of <a href="/wiki/Basse-Terre" title="Basse-Terre">Basse-Terre</a> measured 6.4&#160;in (163&#160;mm).<sup id="cite_ref-rainfall_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainfall-80">[80]</a></sup> Even greater quantities fell at higher elevations of Basse Terre Island, with a maximum total of 18.07&#160;in (459&#160;mm) measured at the mountainous locality of <a href="/wiki/Matouba" title="Matouba">Matouba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint-Claude,_Guadeloupe" title="Saint-Claude, Guadeloupe">Saint-Claude</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupemeteo_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupemeteo-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the archipelago, the hurricane left 40% of the population (80,000 households) without power and 25% of landline users without service.<sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-81">[81]</a></sup> The islands of <a href="/wiki/Marie-Galante" title="Marie-Galante">Marie-Galante</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a> and especially <a href="/wiki/Les_Saintes" class="mw-redirect" title="Les Saintes">Les Saintes</a> bore the brunt of the winds, which caused heavy damage to structures and nature alike and cut the islands off from their surroundings for several days.<sup id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-81">[81]</a></sup> Homes on <a href="/wiki/Terre-de-Haut_Island" title="Terre-de-Haut Island">Terre-de-Haut Island</a> of Les Saintes were flooded or lost their roofs.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> On the mainland, sections of Pointe-à-Pitre stood under more than 3.3&#160;feet (1&#160;m) of water, and the city's hospital sustained significant damage.<sup id="cite_ref-interieur_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-83">[83]</a></sup> The Basse-Terre region suffered severe damage to nearly 100% of its banana crops, comrpising a total area of more than 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Acre" title="Acre">acres</a> (2,000 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a>); farmers described the destruction to their plantations as "complete annihilation".<sup id="cite_ref-cropsfrench_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cropsfrench-84">[84]</a></sup> Beyond their impact on farmland, the strong winds ravaged much of the island's vegetation: fallen trees and branches covered practically every major road and were responsible for one death.<sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-81">[81]</a></sup> Another person was killed upon being swept out to sea.<sup id="cite_ref-MariaGuadeloupe_57-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MariaGuadeloupe-57">[57]</a></sup> Two people disappeared at sea after their vessel capsized offshore <a href="/wiki/La_D%C3%A9sirade" title="La Désirade">La Désirade</a>, east of mainland <a href="/wiki/Grande-Terre" title="Grande-Terre">Grande-Terre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guadeloupetrees_81-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guadeloupetrees-81">[81]</a></sup> Damage from Maria across Guadeloupe amounted to at least €100 million (US$120 million).<sup id="cite_ref-dmgguadeloupe_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dmgguadeloupe-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Martinique">Martinique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Martinique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Passing 30&#160;mi (50&#160;km) off the northern shorelines, Maria brought torrential rainfall and strong gusts to Martinique but spared the island of its hurricane-force windfield,<sup id="cite_ref-frenchislands_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-86">[86]</a></sup> which at the time extended 25&#160;mi (35&#160;km) around the eye.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> The commune of <a href="/wiki/Le_Marigot" title="Le Marigot">Le Marigot</a> recorded 6.7&#160;inches (170&#160;mm) of rain over a 24-hour period.<sup id="cite_ref-rainfall_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainfall-80">[80]</a></sup> By September 19, Maria had knocked out power to 70,000 households, about 40% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-lci_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lci-88">[88]</a></sup> Water service was cut to 50,000 customers, especially in the communes of <a href="/wiki/Le_Morne-Rouge" title="Le Morne-Rouge">Le Morne-Rouge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gros-Morne,_Martinique" title="Gros-Morne, Martinique">Gros-Morne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-frenchislands_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-interieur_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-83">[83]</a></sup> Numerous roads and streets, especially along the northern coast, were impassible due to rock slides, fallen trees and toppled power poles.<sup id="cite_ref-interieur_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lci_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lci-88">[88]</a></sup> Streets in <a href="/wiki/Fort-de-France" title="Fort-de-France">Fort-de-France</a> were inundated.<sup id="cite_ref-frenchislands_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-86">[86]</a></sup> In the seaside commune of <a href="/wiki/Le_Carbet" title="Le Carbet">Le Carbet</a>, rough seas washed ashore large rocks and demolished some coastal structures,<sup id="cite_ref-frenchislands_86-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frenchislands-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimescarib_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimescarib-89">[89]</a></sup> while some boats were blown over along the bay of the commune of <a href="/wiki/Sch%C5%93lcher" title="Schœlcher">Schœlcher</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Martinique's agricultural sector suffered considerable losses: about 70% of banana crops sustained wind damage, with nearly every tree downed along the northern coast.<sup id="cite_ref-cropsfrench_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cropsfrench-84">[84]</a></sup> There were no deaths on the island, although four people were injured in the hurricane—two seriously and two lightly.<sup id="cite_ref-interieur_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-interieur-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States_Virgin_Islands">United States Virgin Islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: United States Virgin Islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Maria's outer eyewall was reported by the National Hurricane Center to have crossed <a href="/wiki/Saint_Croix" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Croix">Saint Croix</a> while the hurricane was at Category 5 intensity. The hurricane caused extensive and severe damage to the island. Sustained winds at the <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Point_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge">Sandy Point National Wildlife Refuge</a> reached 99 to 104&#160;mph (159 to 167&#160;km/h) and gusted to 137&#160;mph (220&#160;km/h).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The Luis Hospital suffered roof damage and flooding, but remained operational.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> One person died from a storm-induced heart attack.<sup id="cite_ref-StCroixHeartAttack_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StCroixHeartAttack-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico_2">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_(2017)_170923-H-NI589-0007_(36602415074).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/220px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/330px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg/440px-Hurricane_Maria_%282017%29_170923-H-NI589-0007_%2836602415074%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_(2017)_170923-H-NI589-0007_(36602415074).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thousands of homes suffered varying degrees of damage while large swaths of vegetation were shredded by the hurricane's violent winds</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A sustained wind of 64&#160;mph (103&#160;km/h) with a gust to 113&#160;mph (182&#160;km/h) was reported in San Juan, Puerto Rico, immediately prior to the hurricane making landfall on the island. After landfall, wind gusts of 109&#160;mph (175&#160;km/h) were reported at Yabucoa Harbor and 118&#160;mph (190&#160;km/h) at Camp Santiago.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> In addition, very heavy rainfall occurred throughout the territory, peaking at 37.9&#160;in (962.7&#160;mm) in <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Widespread flooding affected San Juan, waist-deep in some areas, and numerous structures lost their roof.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> The coastal <a href="/wiki/La_Perla,_San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Perla, San Juan, Puerto Rico">La Perla neighborhood</a> of San Juan was largely destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o" class="mw-redirect" title="Cataño">Cataño</a> saw extensive damage, with the Juana Matos neighborhood estimated to be 80&#160;percent destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Sep21_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Sep21-103">[103]</a></sup> The primary airport in San Juan, the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn_International_Airport" title="Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport">Luis Muñoz Marín International Airport</a>, was slated to reopen on September 22, "offering hurricane victims a chance to flee."<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Storm_surge" title="Storm surge">Storm surge</a> and flash flooding—stemming from flood gate releases at La Plata Lake Dam—converged on the town of <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>, trapping thousands of residents. Survivors indicate that flood waters rose at least 6&#160;ft (1.8&#160;m) in 30&#160;minutes, with flood waters reaching a depth of 15&#160;ft (4.6&#160;m) in some areas. More than 2,000&#160;people were rescued once military relief reached the town 24&#160;hours after the storm. At least eight people died due to the flooding while many are unaccounted for.<sup id="cite_ref-ToaBaja_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ToaBaja-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The hurricane completely destroyed the island's power grid, leaving all 3.4&#160;million residents without electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_Sep21_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Sep21-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Puerto Rican governor <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rosselló">Ricardo Rosselló</a> stated that it could take months to restore power in some locations,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> with San Juan Mayor <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Yul%C3%ADn_Cruz" title="Carmen Yulín Cruz">Carmen Yulín Cruz</a> estimating that some areas would remain without power for four to six months.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Communication networks were crippled across the island; 95.2&#160;percent of cell networks were down with 48 of the island's 78 counties networks being completely inoperable. Only one radio station, <a href="/wiki/WAPA_(AM)" title="WAPA (AM)">WAPA 680 AM</a>, remain on-air through the storm.<sup id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div id="mwe_player_2" class="PopUpMediaTransform" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:854px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_3&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm/854px--Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm.jpg&quot; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hurricane_Maria_at_Coast_Guard_Sector_San_Juan.webm" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hurricane Maria at Coast Guard Sector San Juan</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The nearby island of <a href="/wiki/Vieques" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieques">Vieques</a> suffered similarly extensive damage. Communications were largely lost across the island. Widespread property destruction took place with many structures leveled.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The recreational ship <i>Ferrel</i> carrying a family of four issued a distress signal while battling 20&#160;ft (6.1&#160;m) seas and 115&#160;mph (185&#160;km/h) winds on September&#160;20.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrel_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrel-111">[111]</a></sup> Communications with the vessel were lost near Vieques on September&#160;20. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">United States Coast Guard</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Royal_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="British Royal Navy">British Royal Navy</a> conducted search-and-rescue operations utilizing an <a href="/wiki/HC-130" class="mw-redirect" title="HC-130">HC-130</a> aircraft, a fast response cutter, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Kearsarge_(LHD-3)" title="USS Kearsarge (LHD-3)">USS <i>Kearsarge</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/RFA_Mounts_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="RFA Mounts Bay">RFA Mounts Bay</a> and Navy helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> On September&#160;21, the mother and her two children were rescued while the father drowned inside the capsized vessel.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrel_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrel-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maria's Category 4 winds broke a 96-foot line feed antenna of the <a href="/wiki/Arecibo_Observatory" title="Arecibo Observatory">Arecibo Observatory</a>, causing it to fall 500 feet and puncturing the dish below, greatly reducing its ability to function until repairs can be made.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> On September 24, Governor Rosselló estimated that the damage from Hurricane Maria in Puerto Rico was over $8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-tallies_up_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tallies_up-115">[115]</a></sup> Approximately 80&#160;percent of the territory's agriculture was lost due to the hurricane, with losses estimated at $780&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> As of September 25, the death toll on Puerto Rico stood at 24.<sup id="cite_ref-deathtollPR_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deathtollPR-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominican_Republic">Dominican Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Dominican Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Torrential rains and strong winds impacted the Dominican Republic as Maria tracked northeast of the country. Assessments on September&#160;22 indicate 110&#160;homes were destroyed, 570 were damaged, and 3,723 were affected by flooding. Approximately 60,000&#160;people lost power in northern areas of the country. Flooding and landslides rendered many roads impassable, cutting off 38&#160;communities.<sup id="cite_ref-EC_Sep22_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC_Sep22-55">[55]</a></sup> Two people were killed, one from a landslide and the other by a fallen tree, and another was reported missing.<sup id="cite_ref-DRtwodeaths_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DRtwodeaths-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominica_2">Dominica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dominica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Through the Caribbean Catastrophe Risk Insurance Facility, Dominica received approximately US$19.2&#160;million in emergency funds.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(LHD-1)" title="USS Wasp (LHD-1)">USS <i>Wasp</i></a>, previously deployed to <a href="/wiki/Saint_Martin" title="Saint Martin">Saint Martin</a> to assist in relief efforts after Hurricane Irma, arrived in Dominica on September&#160;22. The vessel carried two <a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_SH-60_Seahawk" title="Sikorsky SH-60 Seahawk">Sikorsky SH-60 Seahawk</a> helicopters to assist in distribution of relief supplies in hard-to-reach areas.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> on September&#160;23, Prime Minister Skerrit called the situation in Dominica an "international humanitarian emergency".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Puerto_Rico_3">Puerto Rico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Puerto Rico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg/310px-DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg" width="310" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg/465px-DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg/620px-DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="512" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DKlJzVnXoAEu2Pt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Comparison of lights at night in Puerto Rico before <i>(top)</i> and after <i>(bottom)</i> Hurricane Maria.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The power grid was effectively destroyed, leaving millions without electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-Power_grid_destroyed._121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Power_grid_destroyed.-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<table class="rquote floatright" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:right; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">There's a humanitarian emergency here in Puerto Rico.... This is an event without precedent.</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;"><cite>—&#160;<a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Rossell%C3%B3" title="Ricardo Rosselló">Ricardo Rosselló</a><sup id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-122">[122]</a></sup></cite></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The entirety of Puerto Rico was declared a federal disaster zone shortly after the hurricane.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-122">[122]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> planned to open an air bridge with three to four aircraft carrying essential supplies to the island daily starting on September&#160;22.<sup id="cite_ref-NBCNY_Sep22_106-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NBCNY_Sep22-106">[106]</a></sup> The territory's government contracted 56&#160;small companies to assist in restoring power.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_Sep22_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_Sep22-122">[122]</a></sup> Commercial traffic resumed at Luis Muñoz Marín International on September&#160;22, with <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> being the first to restore connections. The airline provided food, water, lanterns, cots, tarps, fans, batteries, boots, and generators to employees and their families in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Guajataca_Lake" title="Guajataca Lake">Guajataca Dam</a> was structurally damaged, and on September&#160;22, the National Weather Service issued a <a href="/wiki/Flash_flood_emergency" class="mw-redirect" title="Flash flood emergency">flash flood emergency</a> for parts of the area in response.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Tens of thousands of people were ordered to evacuate the area, with about 70,000 thought to be at risk.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Federal aid arrived en-masse on September&#160;25 with the reopening of major ports. Eleven cargo vessels collectively carrying 1.3&#160;million liters of water, 23,000&#160;cots, and dozens of generators.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>An economist estimated that Maria left at least <a href="/wiki/US$" class="mw-redirect" title="US$">US$</a> 50 billion in damage.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">
<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">
<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/32px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/48px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG/64px-Cyclone_Catarina_from_the_ISS_on_March_26_2004.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3032" data-file-height="2004" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Tropical_cyclones" title="Portal:Tropical cyclones">Tropical cyclones portal</a></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_Category_5_Atlantic_hurricanes" title="List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes">List of Category 5 Atlantic hurricanes</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_David" title="Hurricane David">Hurricane David</a> in 1979 – one of the deadliest tropical cyclones to hit Dominica</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erika" title="Tropical Storm Erika">Tropical Storm Erika</a> in 2015 – devastated the island of Dominica with severe flooding</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Georges" title="Hurricane Georges">Hurricane Georges</a> in 1998 – the last major hurricane to strike Puerto Rico</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> in 1989 – the last category 4 hurricane to strike Saint Croix</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Luis" title="Hurricane Luis">Hurricane Luis</a> in 1995 – brought severe damage to several islands of the Lesser Antilles</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marilyn" title="Hurricane Marilyn">Hurricane Marilyn</a> in 1995 – affected Dominica and Guadeloupe and brought severe damage to the U.S. Virgin Islands</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hortense" title="Hurricane Hortense">Hurricane Hortense</a> in 1996 – affected Puerto Rico and caused widespread flooding across the island</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joaquin" title="Hurricane Joaquin">Hurricane Joaquin</a> in 2015 – approached the <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">Southeast US</a> coastline and interacted with another storm to the west, triggering historic flooding over the region</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hurricane_Maria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
